         \u2502                 \u2502 Execute Task  \u2502\n       \u2502                   \u2502                  \u2502                 \u2502                 \u2502 (Training)    \u2502\n       \u2502                   \u2502                  \u2502                 \u2502                 \u2502                \u2502\n```\n\n### 3.2 Step-by-Step Code Trace\n\n#### Step 1: Drift Detection (`drift_detector.c/h`)\n\nThe `DriftDetector` continuously monitors model metrics. When a metric exceeds the configured threshold, drift is detected.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.c`, lines 177-234\n\n```c\nint drift_detector_update_metric(const char *model_id, double metric_value) {\n    // ... lookup model state ...\n\n    // Page-Hinkley test computation\n    state->cumulative_sum += (metric_value - state->x_mean - state->delta);\n    double ph_statistic = state->cumulative_sum - state->min_cumulative_sum;\n\n    // Drift detected?\n    if (ph_statistic > state->lambda) {\n        char reason[128];\n        snprintf(reason, sizeof(reason),\n                 \"Drift detected (PH=%.4f > \u03bb=%.4f) after %zu samples\",\n                 ph_statistic, state->lambda, state->sample_count);\n\n        // Notify observers (releases lock first to avoid deadlocks)\n        callback_node_t *tmp_callbacks = g_callbacks;\n        pthread_mutex_unlock(&g_lock);\n\n        while (tmp_callbacks) {\n            tmp_callbacks->fn(model_id, reason, tmp_callbacks->user_data);\n            tmp_callbacks = tmp_callbacks->next;\n        }\n        // ... reset state for next cycle ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe drift detector uses the **Page-Hinkley test** for change detection and notifies all registered callbacks when drift exceeds `lambda`.\n\n#### Step 2: Model Monitor Aggregation (`model_monitor.c/h`)\n\nThe `ModelMonitor` aggregates monitoring events and performs periodic surveillance. It detects drift based on accuracy/loss thresholds.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c`, lines 191-233\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg) {\n    ll_model_monitor *mon = arg;\n\n    while (mon->running) {\n        double live_acc = 0.0, live_loss = 0.0;\n        long   ts       = 0L;\n\n        if (!acquire_live_metrics(mon, &live_acc, &live_loss, &ts)) {\n            goto sleep_and_continue;\n        }\n\n        if (drift_detected(mon, live_acc, live_loss)) {\n            ll_drift_event ev = {\n                .model_id         = mon->model_id,\n                .live_accuracy    = live_acc,\n                .live_loss        = live_loss,\n                .baseline_accuracy= mon->baseline_accuracy,\n                .baseline_loss    = mon->baseline_loss,\n                .timestamp        = ts\n            };\n\n            ll_log_warn(\"[Monitor:%s] DRIFT detected (live_acc=%.4f, baseline=%.4f)\",\n                        mon->model_id, live_acc, mon->baseline_accuracy);\n\n            notify_observers(mon, &ev);  // Notify registered observers\n\n            if (mon->cfg.auto_refresh_baseline)\n                refresh_baseline(mon);\n        }\n        sleep_interrupible(mon->cfg.poll_interval_sec);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Retraining Trigger Evaluation (`retraining_trigger.c/h`)\n\nThe `RetrainingTrigger` component decides whether retraining is warranted based on drift severity and policy rules.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.c`, lines 343-400\n\n```c\nstatic bool _rt_drift_detected(rt_model_entry_t *ent) {\n    if (ent->count < RT_BASELINE_WINDOW * 2) { return false; }\n\n    double baseline = _rt_avg_first_n(ent, RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n    double current  = _rt_avg_last_n(ent,  RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n\n    if (baseline == 0.0) { return false; }\n\n    double delta_pct;\n    if (ent->metric_type == RT_METRIC_LOSS) {\n        // Increase in loss indicates drift\n        delta_pct = ((current - baseline) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    } else {\n        // Decrease in metric (accuracy, F1, etc.) indicates drift\n        delta_pct = ((baseline - current) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    }\n}\n\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void) {\n    // ... scan registry for drift ...\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i) {\n        if (_rt_drift_detected(ent)) {\n            ent->retrain_pending = true;\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n            bool ok = _rt_state.callback(ent->model_id);  // Trigger retraining\n\n            pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n            if (ok) {\n                ent->count = 0;\n                ent->head = 0;\n                ent->retrain_pending = false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Orchestrator Receives Drift Event (`orchestrator.c`)\n\nThe main orchestrator subscribes to drift events and initiates retraining when notified.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/orchestrator.c`, lines 266-307\n\n```c\nstatic void *scheduler_mainloop(void *arg) {\n    const int interval_hours = g_orch.cfg.retrain_interval_hours;\n\n    while (1) {\n        if (!keep_running) break;\n\n        // Wait for either drift alert or time-based trigger\n        scheduler_wait_or_timeout(interval_hours * 3600);\n\n        // Consume any pending drift events\n        if (observer_drift_detected()) {\n            LL_LOG_INFO(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG,\n                        \"Model drift detected \u2013 initiating immediate retraining.\");\n        }\n\n        if (start_training_pipeline() != 0) {\n            LL_LOG_ERROR(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG, \"Scheduled training failed; will retry later.\");\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Pipeline Manager Constructs Training Pipeline (`pipeline_manager.c`)\n\nThe Pipeline Manager coordinates the retraining workflow.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.c`, lines 252-283\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg) {\n    pipeline_manager_t *pmgr = (pipeline_manager_t *)arg;\n\n    // Subscribe to drift events\n    drift_event_handle_t handle = drift_detector_subscribe(pmgr->drift_detector);\n\n    while (pmgr->running) {\n        drift_event_t event;\n        if (drift_detector_await_event(handle, &event, 30 /* sec timeout */) < 0)\n            continue;\n\n        if (event.type == DRIFT_EVENT_TYPE_DRIFT_DETECTED) {\n            LOG_WARN(\"Data or model drift detected => triggering retraining\");\n\n            pthread_mutex_lock(&pmgr->state_mtx);\n            bool ok = trigger_training_locked(pmgr, \"drift-detected\");\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&pmgr->state_mtx);\n\n            if (!ok)\n                LOG_ERROR(\"Monitor loop retraining request failed\");\n\n            safe_sleep_sec(RETRAINING_BACKOFF_SEC);  // Cooldown period\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Job Factory Creates Training Job (`job_factory.c/h`)\n\nThe Job Factory uses the **Factory Pattern** to create a training job with proper metadata.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h`, lines 46-55\n\n```c\ntypedef enum {\n    LL_JOB_TRAIN_MODEL = 0,       // First-time supervised training\n    LL_JOB_HYPERPARAM_TUNE,       // Hyper-parameter optimization\n    LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL,         // Triggered by concept drift\n    LL_JOB_DATA_PREPROCESS,       // Batch or incremental ETL\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_MONITOR,         // Metrics/alert job\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_VERSION_ROLLOUT, // Canary or blue-green deployment\n} ll_job_kind_e;\n```\n\n**Pipeline Manager calling Job Factory** (`pipeline_manager.c`, lines 296-338):\n```c\nstatic bool trigger_training_locked(pipeline_manager_t *pmgr, const char *reason) {\n    // Build the Training Job via Factory Pattern\n    training_job_t *job = training_job_factory_create(pmgr->job_factory, reason);\n\n    if (!job) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"training_job_factory_create failed\");\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    // Register experiment with Model Registry\n    char exp_id[MODEL_REGISTRY_MAX_ID];\n    if (model_registry_create_experiment(pmgr->registry, job, reason, exp_id, sizeof(exp_id)) < 0) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"Failed to log experiment into Model Registry\");\n        training_job_destroy(job);\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    LOG_INFO(\"Experiment '%s' registered, launching training job\", exp_id);\n\n    // Execute the training job\n    if (training_job_execute(job) != 0) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"Training job execution failed for experiment '%s'\", exp_id);\n        model_registry_update_status(pmgr->registry, exp_id, MODEL_STATUS_FAILED);\n        training_job_destroy(job);\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    // Persist success status to registry\n    model_registry_update_status(pmgr->registry, exp_id, MODEL_STATUS_SUCCEEDED);\n    LOG_INFO(\"Training completed successfully for experiment '%s'\", exp_id);\n    training_job_destroy(job);\n    return true;\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Task Scheduler Executes Job (`task_scheduler.c/h`)\n\nThe Task Scheduler manages job execution with worker threads.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h`, lines 173-181\n\n```c\nint lxl_task_scheduler_schedule(lxl_task_scheduler_t *scheduler,\n                                const char           *task_id,\n                                const char           *task_name,\n                                lxl_task_fn_t         cb,\n                                void                 *user_ctx,\n                                time_t                first_run,\n                                uint32_t              interval_sec,\n                                int                   priority);\n```\n\nThe scheduler provides priority-based task execution with worker threads, observer notifications for task lifecycle events (`LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_START`, `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_SUCCESS`, etc.).\n\n### 3.3 Workflow Summary\n\n| Step | Component | File | Key Function |\n|------|-----------|------|--------------|\n| 1 | Drift Detector | `drift_detector.c` | `drift_detector_update_metric()` |\n| 2 | Model Monitor | `model_monitor.c` | `monitor_loop()` \u2192 `notify_observers()` |\n| 3 | Retraining Trigger | `retraining_trigger.c` | `rt_check_and_schedule()` |\n| 4 | Orchestrator | `orchestrator.c` | `scheduler_mainloop()` \u2192 `start_training_pipeline()` |\n| 5 | Pipeline Manager | `pipeline_manager.c` | `trigger_training_locked()` |\n| 6 | Job Factory | `job_factory.c` | `job_factory_create()` |\n| 7 | Task Scheduler | `task_scheduler.c` | `lxl_task_scheduler_schedule_once()` |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Critical Analysis of MVC Pattern Usage\n\n### 4.1 Benefits of MVC in This Context\n\n#### 4.1.1 Strong Separation of Concerns\n\n**Evidence**: The directory structure (`src/model/`, `src/view/`, `src/controller/`) creates clear boundaries between:\n- ML algorithm logic (Model)\n- Dashboard presentation (View)\n- Pipeline orchestration (Controller)\n\n**Impact**: A developer can modify the transformer model implementation (`transformer_summarizer.c`) without touching any Controller or View code. Similarly, adding a new dashboard endpoint requires no Model layer changes.\n\n#### 4.1.2 Modularity and Extensibility via Strategy Pattern\n\n**Evidence** (from `model_strategy.h`, lines 99-104):\n```c\ntypedef struct model_strategy {\n    const char *name;\n    const struct model_strategy_vtable *vptr;  // Virtual table\n    void *impl;\n} model_strategy_t;\n```\n\n**Impact**: New ML strategies can be added by:\n1. Implementing a new strategy file (e.g., `bert_classifier.c`)\n2. Registering it via `ll_strategy_register(\"bert_classifier\", bert_ctor);`\n3. Updating `orchestrator.toml` to specify `active = \"bert_classifier\"`\n\nNo Controller recompilation required - this is a significant MLOps benefit.\n\n#### 4.1.3 Clear High-Level Structure for Complex Systems\n\n**Evidence**: The architecture diagram in `docs/architecture.md` (lines 25-43) provides immediate visual understanding of system organization.\n\n**Impact**: Onboarding new developers is simplified because the MVC pattern is widely understood. The mental model transfers well even though this is a backend system rather than a traditional web application.\n\n#### 4.1.4 Observer Pattern Decouples Components\n\n**Evidence** (from `observer.h`, lines 206-216):\n```c\nstatic inline void observable_notify(const observable_t *observable,\n                                     const observer_event_t *event) {\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < observable->count; ++i) {\n        observer_t *sub = observable->subscribers[i];\n        if (sub && sub->on_event)\n            sub->on_event(event, sub->user_data);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Impact**: Drift detection, logging, dashboard updates, and retraining triggers can all respond to the same event without explicit coupling. Adding a new consumer (e.g., Slack alerts) requires only registering a new observer.\n\n#### 4.1.5 Factory Pattern Enables MLOps Compliance\n\n**Evidence**: The `job_factory.c/h` creates jobs with full metadata for reproducibility:\n- `job_id`, `submitted_by`, `created_at`, `tags[]`\n- JSON serialization for audit trails (`job_factory_to_json()`)\n\n**Impact**: Every training run is traceable, which is essential for ML governance and debugging production issues.\n\n### 4.2 Drawbacks and Architectural Concerns\n\n#### 4.2.1 MVC Mismatch: User Interaction vs. Event-Driven Backend\n\n**Issue**: MVC was designed for interactive user applications with request-response cycles. This ML orchestrator is a long-running, event-driven backend process.\n\n**Evidence of Strain**: The \"View\" (`dashboard_server.c`) is essentially a metrics push server, not a traditional UI. The comment in `dashboard_server.c` (lines 11-18) acknowledges this:\n```c\n/*\n * This module belongs to the View layer and exposes a lightweight HTTP\n * endpoint that streams real-time model-monitoring information to\n * JavaScript dashboards.  The server is intentionally kept simple...\n */\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The View's role is minimal and stretched conceptually\n- No actual \"user input\" handling in the traditional MVC sense\n- The pattern metaphor breaks down when explaining the system to newcomers unfamiliar with this non-standard usage\n\n#### 4.2.2 Controller Bloat (\"Fat Controller\" Anti-Pattern)\n\n**Issue**: The Controller layer contains excessive logic because it must manage:\n- Pipeline orchestration (`pipeline_manager.c`: 359 lines)\n- Drift detection (`drift_detector.c`: 320 lines)\n- Model monitoring (`model_monitor.c`: 365 lines)\n- Task scheduling (`task_scheduler.c`: 400+ lines)\n- Job factory (`job_factory.c`: 300+ lines)\n- Retraining triggers (`retraining_trigger.c`: 415 lines)\n\n**Evidence**: The Controller directory has **6 subdirectories** and **16 files** compared to the Model's **4 subdirectories** and **12 files**.\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The Controller becomes a \"god object\" that knows too much\n- Testing the Controller requires mocking numerous dependencies\n- Changes to orchestration logic risk cascading effects\n\n#### 4.2.3 C Language Limitations for MVC Implementation\n\n**Issue**: MVC frameworks in higher-level languages (Rails, Django, Spring) provide:\n- Automatic dependency injection\n- Data binding between Model and View\n- Declarative routing\n- AOP for cross-cutting concerns\n\nIn C, all of this must be implemented manually.\n\n**Evidence of Manual Wiring** (from `main.c`, lines 563-574):\n```c\nPipelineCtx pipeline_ctx = { .cfg = &cfg,\n                             .registry = &registry,\n                             .strategy = strategy };\n\nScheduler scheduler = { .cfg = &cfg, .pipeline = &pipeline_ctx };\nif (!scheduler_start(&scheduler)) {\n    LOG_ERROR(\"Failed to start scheduler.\");\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- Boilerplate code for wiring components\n- No runtime reflection for flexible component discovery\n- Callback-based Observer pattern is verbose and error-prone (risk of callback hell)\n\n#### 4.2.4 Communication Overhead in C\n\n**Issue**: Model-to-Controller communication via callbacks can be awkward:\n\n**Evidence** (from `drift_detector.c`, lines 213-222):\n```c\n// Provide callback outside of locked section to avoid deadlocks.\ncallback_node_t *tmp_callbacks = g_callbacks;\npthread_mutex_unlock(&g_lock);\n\n// Notify observers\nwhile (tmp_callbacks) {\n    tmp_callbacks->fn(model_id, reason, tmp_callbacks->user_data);\n    tmp_callbacks = tmp_callbacks->next;\n}\n\n// Reacquire lock to reset state.\npthread_mutex_lock(&g_lock);\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- Manual lock management to avoid deadlocks\n- No built-in async/await or message queues\n- Potential for subtle concurrency bugs\n\n#### 4.2.5 View Layer Underutilization\n\n**Issue**: The View layer contains only **2 files** (`dashboard_server.c/h`), suggesting it's architecturally under-weighted.\n\n**Evidence**: The View's primary function is to expose `/api/metrics` - a simple JSON endpoint. This could reasonably be a Controller-adjacent utility rather than a separate architectural layer.\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The \"V\" in MVC feels forced in this context\n- Creates artificial separation for minimal benefit\n- May confuse developers expecting a richer View layer\n\n### 4.3 Alternative Patterns to Consider\n\n| Pattern | Suitability | Rationale |\n|---------|------------|-----------|\n| **Hexagonal Architecture (Ports & Adapters)** | High | Better fit for external service integration (LMS API, Feature Store, Model Registry) |\n| **Event-Driven Architecture** | High | Natural fit for drift detection \u2192 retraining workflows |\n| **Pipeline Pattern (alone)** | Medium | Already used internally; could be the primary organizational principle |\n| **Actor Model** | Medium | Mentioned in `docs/architecture.md` (line 116); better for concurrent, message-passing systems |\n\n### 4.4 Summary Assessment\n\n| Aspect | Rating | Justification |\n|--------|--------|--------------|\n| Separation of Concerns | **Good** | Clear boundaries between ML logic, orchestration, and presentation |\n| Extensibility | **Good** | Strategy Pattern allows runtime algorithm swapping |\n| Pattern Fit | **Fair** | MVC's interactive metaphor is stretched for event-driven backends |\n| Controller Complexity | **Concerning** | Risk of \"fat controller\" anti-pattern |\n| Implementation Overhead | **Concerning** | C requires manual wiring that MVC frameworks automate |\n| View Utilization | **Poor** | Minimal View layer suggests pattern mismatch |\n\n**Overall Verdict**: The MVC pattern provides useful organizational structure for this complex system, particularly through its clear directory hierarchy and Strategy Pattern integration. However, the pattern is being used outside its traditional domain (interactive UIs), leading to a stretched View metaphor and bloated Controller. For future evolution, consider migrating toward a Hexagonal or Event-Driven architecture while preserving the existing Strategy and Observer patterns.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conclusion\n\nThe LexiLearn Orchestrator demonstrates a pragmatic adaptation of MVC to the ML orchestration domain. The architecture succeeds in:\n\n1. **Separating ML algorithms** (Model) from **orchestration logic** (Controller) from **external communication** (View)\n2. **Enabling runtime extensibility** through Strategy and Factory patterns\n3. **Decoupling event producers and consumers** via the Observer pattern\n\nHowever, the architecture shows strain in:\n\n1. **The View layer's minimal role**, suggesting MVC's interactive model doesn't fully translate\n2. **Controller complexity**, which risks becoming unmanageable as the system grows\n3. **Manual C-language wiring**, which increases boilerplate compared to framework-supported MVC\n\nFor teams maintaining this system, the recommendations are:\n\n- **Short-term**: Continue using the existing structure but guard against Controller bloat by extracting services\n- **Medium-term**: Introduce message queues (e.g., ZeroMQ) for Model-Controller communication to formalize the event-driven nature\n- **Long-term**: Consider evolving toward Hexagonal Architecture or a pure Event-Sourced design that better matches the system's actual communication patterns\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Key File Reference\n\n| Layer | Key Files | Purpose |\n|-------|-----------|---------|\n| **Model** | `model_strategy.h` | Strategy interface definition |\n| | `model_trainer.h/.c` | Training coordination |\n| | `model_registry.h/.c` | Artifact versioning |\n| | `feature_store_manager.h/.c` | Feature persistence |\n| **View** | `dashboard_server.h/.c` | HTTP metrics endpoint |\n| **Controller** | `orchestrator.h/.c` | Central coordinator |\n| | `pipeline_manager.h/.c` | Pipeline orchestration |\n| | `drift_detector.h/.c` | Drift detection logic |\n| | `model_monitor.h/.c` | Performance surveillance |\n| | `retraining_trigger.h/.c` | Retraining policy |\n| | `observer.h` | Observer Pattern infrastructure |\n| | `job_factory.h/.c` | Factory Pattern for jobs |\n| | `task_scheduler.h/.c` | Task execution engine |\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

  "content": "# LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator - Architectural Analysis\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe LexiLearn Orchestrator is a C-based ML pipeline management system that adopts the Model-View-Controller (MVC) architectural pattern. This document provides a comprehensive analysis of the architecture, mapping components to MVC roles, describing communication pathways, tracing the critical drift-to-retraining workflow, and offering a critical assessment of this architectural choice.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Component Mapping to MVC Roles\n\n### 1.1 Model Layer (`src/model/`)\n\nThe Model layer encapsulates all machine learning domain logic, data processing, and state management. It is responsible for the \"business logic\" of the ML system - the actual algorithms, data transformations, and persistent storage of ML artifacts.\n\n| Directory/File | Purpose | MVC Role Justification |\n|---------------|---------|----------------------|\n| `src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h` | Strategy Pattern interface for ML algorithms | Defines interchangeable ML algorithm contracts |\n| `src/model/ml_models/transformer_summarizer.c/h` | Transformer-based summarization | Concrete ML strategy implementation |\n| `src/model/ml_models/ngram_analyzer.c/h` | N-gram-based text analysis | Concrete ML strategy implementation |\n| `src/model/ml_models/hybrid_model.c/h` | Ensemble/hybrid modeling | Concrete ML strategy implementation |\n| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_trainer.c/h` | Coordinates training workflows | Training execution engine |\n| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_registry.c/h` | Model versioning and artifact storage | Persistent state management |\n| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_evaluator.c/h` | Model quality assessment | Evaluation logic |\n| `src/model/ml_pipeline/experiment_tracker.c/h` | Experiment lineage tracking | Audit trail management |\n| `src/model/preprocessing/tokenizer.c/h` | Text tokenization | Data transformation |\n| `src/model/preprocessing/text_cleaner.c/h` | Text normalization | Data transformation |\n| `src/model/feature_store/feature_store_manager.c/h` | Feature persistence and retrieval | Feature data management |\n\n**Key Model Layer Characteristics:**\n- **Strategy Pattern**: The `model_strategy.h` file defines a vtable-based interface (`model_strategy_vtable_t`) that allows runtime swapping of ML algorithms without Controller changes (lines 113-173 of `model_strategy.h`).\n- **Encapsulation**: All ML-specific logic is isolated from orchestration concerns.\n- **State Management**: The Model Registry (`model_registry.c/h`) handles persistent model artifacts with versioning, stage promotion (Experiment \u2192 Staging \u2192 Production \u2192 Archived), and lineage tracking.\n\n### 1.2 View Layer (`src/view/`)\n\nThe View layer handles presentation and user/external system communication. In this ML orchestrator context, the \"View\" is non-traditional - it's a data server rather than a GUI.\n\n| Directory/File | Purpose | MVC Role Justification |\n|---------------|---------|----------------------|\n| `src/view/dashboard_server.c/h` | HTTP/WebSocket server for dashboards | Exposes system state to external consumers |\n\n**Key View Layer Characteristics:**\n- **Dashboard Server** (`dashboard_server.c`): An HTTP server using libmicrohttpd that exposes real-time metrics via `/api/metrics` endpoint (lines 103-205).\n- **Observer Consumer**: The View subscribes to Controller events and pushes metrics updates via WebSocket to connected dashboard clients.\n- **Separation of Concerns**: The View does not contain business logic - it only formats and transmits data received from the Controller.\n\n**Relevant API from `dashboard_server.h`:**\n```c\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_publish(DashboardServer *srv,\n                                  const char *channel_name,\n                                  const char *json_payload);  // Push metrics to dashboards\n```\n\n### 1.3 Controller Layer (`src/controller/`)\n\nThe Controller layer orchestrates the entire system, coordinating data flow between Model and View, handling user inputs, and managing the ML pipeline lifecycle.\n\n| Directory/File | Purpose | MVC Role Justification |\n|---------------|---------|----------------------|\n| `src/controller/orchestrator.c/h` | Central orchestration coordinator | Main Controller - coordinates all components |\n| `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.c/h` | ML pipeline lifecycle management | Pipeline orchestration |\n| `src/controller/pipeline/ingestion_stage.c/h` | Data ingestion coordination | ETL stage management |\n| `src/controller/pipeline/training_stage.c/h` | Training workflow coordination | Training stage management |\n| `src/controller/pipeline/deployment_stage.c/h` | Model deployment coordination | Deployment stage management |\n| `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.c/h` | Statistical drift detection | Monitoring component |\n| `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c/h` | Model performance surveillance | Monitoring aggregation |\n| `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.c/h` | Automated retraining decisions | Retraining policy enforcement |\n| `src/controller/monitoring/observer.h` | Observer Pattern infrastructure | Event dispatch mechanism |\n| `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.c/h` | Task scheduling engine | Job execution coordination |\n| `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.c/h` | Training job creation (Factory Pattern) | Job instantiation |\n| `src/controller/job_factory/job_types.h` | Job type definitions | Job taxonomy |\n\n**Key Controller Layer Characteristics:**\n- **Orchestrator** (`orchestrator.c`): The central coordinator that initializes subsystems, manages the scheduler thread, and executes the training pipeline (see `start_training_pipeline()` at lines 170-257 of `orchestrator.c`).\n- **Observer Pattern Hub**: The Controller hosts the Observer infrastructure (`observer.h`) that decouples event producers from consumers.\n- **Factory Pattern**: The `job_factory.c/h` creates various job types (`LL_JOB_TRAIN_MODEL`, `LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL`, etc.) without exposing creation details.\n- **Pipeline Pattern**: The `pipeline_manager.c` composes discrete stages (ingestion \u2192 training \u2192 deployment \u2192 monitoring).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Communication Pathways Between MVC Layers\n\n### 2.1 Controller \u2192 Model Communication (Imperative Commands)\n\nThe Controller layer invokes Model layer functions directly through well-defined C APIs. This is a synchronous, command-based interaction pattern.\n\n**Example Flow: Training Initiation**\n\nFrom `orchestrator.c` (lines 222-236):\n```c\n// 4. engineered features\n\n### 2.2 Model \u2192 Controller Communication (Observer Pattern)\n\nModel layer components notify the Controller of state changes through the Observer Pattern, avoiding tight coupling.\n\n**Observer Infrastructure** (`observer.h`, lines 93-102):\n```c\ntypedef void (*observer_callback_t)(const observer_event_t *event,\n                                    void                  *user_data);\n\ntypedef struct observer {\n    char                name[OBSERVER_MAX_NAME_LEN];\n    observer_callback_t on_event;\n    void               *user_data;\n} observer_t;\n```\n\n**Event det->cfg.model_id, LEXI_MODEL_ID_LEN);\n    evt.score     = det->last_score;\n    evt.threshold = det->cfg.threshold;\n    evt.timestamp = time(NULL);\n\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < det->listener_cnt; ++i) {\n        det->listeners[i](&evt, det->listener_ctx[i]);  // Notify registered observers\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Controller \u2192 View Communication (Push Updates)\n\nThe Controller pushes Critical Workflow Trace: Drift Detection to Retraining\n\nThis section traces the complete sequence of events when the `DriftDetector` identifies significant data drift, triggering an automated          \u2502                 \u2502 Execute Task  \u2502\n       \u2502                   \u2502                  \u2502                 \u2502                 \u2502 (Training)    \u2502\n       \u2502                   \u2502                  \u2502                 \u2502                 \u2502                \u2502\n```\n\n### 3.2 Step-by-Step Code Trace\n\n#### Step 1: Drift Detection (`drift_detector.c/h`)\n\nThe `DriftDetector` continuously monitors model metrics. When a metric exceeds the configured threshold, drift is detected.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.c`, lines 177-234\n\n```c\nint drift_detector_update_metric(const char *model_id, double metric_value) {\n    // ... lookup model state ...\n\n    // Page-Hinkley test computation\n    state->cumulative_sum += (metric_value - state->x_mean - state->delta);\n    double ph_statistic = state->cumulative_sum - state->min_cumulative_sum;\n\n    // Drift detected?\n    if (ph_statistic > state->lambda) {\n        char reason[128];\n        snprintf(reason, sizeof(reason),\n                 \"Drift detected (PH=%.4f > \u03bb=%.4f) after %zu samples\",\n                 ph_statistic, state->lambda, state->sample_count);\n\n        // Notify observers (releases lock first to avoid deadlocks)\n        callback_node_t *tmp_callbacks = g_callbacks;\n        pthread_mutex_unlock(&g_lock);\n\n        while (tmp_callbacks) {\n            tmp_callbacks->fn(model_id, reason, tmp_callbacks->user_data);\n            tmp_callbacks = tmp_callbacks->next;\n        }\n        // ... reset state for next cycle ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe drift detector uses the **Page-Hinkley test** for change detection and notifies all registered callbacks when drift exceeds `lambda`.\n\n#### Step 2: Model Monitor Aggregation (`model_monitor.c/h`)\n\nThe `ModelMonitor` aggregates monitoring events and performs periodic surveillance. It detects drift based on accuracy/loss thresholds.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c`, lines 191-233\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg) {\n    ll_model_monitor *mon = arg;\n\n    while (mon->running) {\n        double live_acc = 0.0, live_loss = 0.0;\n        long   ts       = 0L;\n\n        if (!acquire_live_metrics(mon, &live_acc, &live_loss, &ts)) {\n            goto sleep_and_continue;\n        }\n\n        if (drift_detected(mon, live_acc, live_loss)) {\n            ll_drift_event ev = {\n                .model_id         = mon->model_id,\n                .live_accuracy    = live_acc,\n                .live_loss        = live_loss,\n                .baseline_accuracy= mon->baseline_accuracy,\n                .baseline_loss    = mon->baseline_loss,\n                .timestamp        = ts\n            };\n\n            ll_log_warn(\"[Monitor:%s] DRIFT detected (live_acc=%.4f, baseline=%.4f)\",\n                        mon->model_id, live_acc, mon->baseline_accuracy);\n\n            notify_observers(mon, &ev);  // Notify registered observers\n\n            if (mon->cfg.auto_refresh_baseline)\n                refresh_baseline(mon);\n        }\n        sleep_interrupible(mon->cfg.poll_interval_sec);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 3: Retraining Trigger Evaluation (`retraining_trigger.c/h`)\n\nThe `RetrainingTrigger` component decides whether retraining is warranted based on drift severity and policy rules.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.c`, lines 343-400\n\n```c\nstatic bool _rt_drift_detected(rt_model_entry_t *ent) {\n    if (ent->count < RT_BASELINE_WINDOW * 2) { return false; }\n\n    double baseline = _rt_avg_first_n(ent, RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n    double current  = _rt_avg_last_n(ent,  RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n\n    if (baseline == 0.0) { return false; }\n\n    double delta_pct;\n    if (ent->metric_type == RT_METRIC_LOSS) {\n        // Increase in loss indicates drift\n        delta_pct = ((current - baseline) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    } else {\n        // Decrease in metric (accuracy, F1, etc.) indicates drift\n        delta_pct = ((baseline - current) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    }\n}\n\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void) {\n    // ... scan registry for drift ...\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i) {\n        if (_rt_drift_detected(ent)) {\n            ent->retrain_pending = true;\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n            bool ok = _rt_state.callback(ent->model_id);  // Trigger retraining\n\n            pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n            if (ok) {\n                ent->count = 0;\n                ent->head = 0;\n                ent->retrain_pending = false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 4: Orchestrator Receives Drift Event (`orchestrator.c`)\n\nThe main orchestrator subscribes to drift events and initiates retraining when notified.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/orchestrator.c`, lines 266-307\n\n```c\nstatic void *scheduler_mainloop(void *arg) {\n    const int interval_hours = g_orch.cfg.retrain_interval_hours;\n\n    while (1) {\n        if (!keep_running) break;\n\n        // Wait for either drift alert or time-based trigger\n        scheduler_wait_or_timeout(interval_hours * 3600);\n\n        // Consume any pending drift events\n        if (observer_drift_detected()) {\n            LL_LOG_INFO(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG,\n                        \"Model drift detected \u2013 initiating immediate retraining.\");\n        }\n\n        if (start_training_pipeline() != 0) {\n            LL_LOG_ERROR(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG, \"Scheduled training failed; will retry later.\");\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 5: Pipeline Manager Constructs Training Pipeline (`pipeline_manager.c`)\n\nThe Pipeline Manager coordinates the retraining workflow.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.c`, lines 252-283\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg) {\n    pipeline_manager_t *pmgr = (pipeline_manager_t *)arg;\n\n    // Subscribe to drift events\n    drift_event_handle_t handle = drift_detector_subscribe(pmgr->drift_detector);\n\n    while (pmgr->running) {\n        drift_event_t event;\n        if (drift_detector_await_event(handle, &event, 30 /* sec timeout */) < 0)\n            continue;\n\n        if (event.type == DRIFT_EVENT_TYPE_DRIFT_DETECTED) {\n            LOG_WARN(\"Data or model drift detected => triggering retraining\");\n\n            pthread_mutex_lock(&pmgr->state_mtx);\n            bool ok = trigger_training_locked(pmgr, \"drift-detected\");\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&pmgr->state_mtx);\n\n            if (!ok)\n                LOG_ERROR(\"Monitor loop retraining request failed\");\n\n            safe_sleep_sec(RETRAINING_BACKOFF_SEC);  // Cooldown period\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 6: Job Factory Creates Training Job (`job_factory.c/h`)\n\nThe Job Factory uses the **Factory Pattern** to create a training job with proper metadata.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h`, lines 46-55\n\n```c\ntypedef enum {\n    LL_JOB_TRAIN_MODEL = 0,       // First-time supervised training\n    LL_JOB_HYPERPARAM_TUNE,       // Hyper-parameter optimization\n    LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL,         // Triggered by concept drift\n    LL_JOB_DATA_PREPROCESS,       // Batch or incremental ETL\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_MONITOR,         // Metrics/alert job\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_VERSION_ROLLOUT, // Canary or blue-green deployment\n} ll_job_kind_e;\n```\n\n**Pipeline Manager calling Job Factory** (`pipeline_manager.c`, lines 296-338):\n```c\nstatic bool trigger_training_locked(pipeline_manager_t *pmgr, const char *reason) {\n    // Build the Training Job via Factory Pattern\n    training_job_t *job = training_job_factory_create(pmgr->job_factory, reason);\n\n    if (!job) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"training_job_factory_create failed\");\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    // Register experiment with Model Registry\n    char exp_id[MODEL_REGISTRY_MAX_ID];\n    if (model_registry_create_experiment(pmgr->registry, job, reason, exp_id, sizeof(exp_id)) < 0) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"Failed to log experiment into Model Registry\");\n        training_job_destroy(job);\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    LOG_INFO(\"Experiment '%s' registered, launching training job\", exp_id);\n\n    // Execute the training job\n    if (training_job_execute(job) != 0) {\n        LOG_ERROR(\"Training job execution failed for experiment '%s'\", exp_id);\n        model_registry_update_status(pmgr->registry, exp_id, MODEL_STATUS_FAILED);\n        training_job_destroy(job);\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    // Persist success status to registry\n    model_registry_update_status(pmgr->registry, exp_id, MODEL_STATUS_SUCCEEDED);\n    LOG_INFO(\"Training completed successfully for experiment '%s'\", exp_id);\n    training_job_destroy(job);\n    return true;\n}\n```\n\n#### Step 7: Task Scheduler Executes Job (`task_scheduler.c/h`)\n\nThe Task Scheduler manages job execution with worker threads.\n\n**File**: `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h`, lines 173-181\n\n```c\nint lxl_task_scheduler_schedule(lxl_task_scheduler_t *scheduler,\n                                const char           *task_id,\n                                const char           *task_name,\n                                lxl_task_fn_t         cb,\n                                void                 *user_ctx,\n                                time_t                first_run,\n                                uint32_t              interval_sec,\n                                int                   priority);\n```\n\nThe scheduler provides priority-based task execution with worker threads, observer notifications for task lifecycle events (`LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_START`, `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_SUCCESS`, etc.).\n\n### 3.3 Workflow Summary\n\n| Step | Component | File | Key Function |\n|------|-----------|------|--------------|\n| 1 | Drift Detector | `drift_detector.c` | `drift_detector_update_metric()` |\n| 2 | Model Monitor | `model_monitor.c` | `monitor_loop()` \u2192 `notify_observers()` |\n| 3 | Retraining Trigger | `retraining_trigger.c` | `rt_check_and_schedule()` |\n| 4 | Orchestrator | `orchestrator.c` | `scheduler_mainloop()` \u2192 `start_training_pipeline()` |\n| 5 | Pipeline Manager | `pipeline_manager.c` | `trigger_training_locked()` |\n| 6 | Job Factory | `job_factory.c` | `job_factory_create()` |\n| 7 | Task Scheduler | `task_scheduler.c` | `lxl_task_scheduler_schedule_once()` |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Critical Analysis of MVC Pattern Usage\n\n### 4.1 Benefits of MVC in This Context\n\n#### 4.1.1 Strong Separation of Concerns\n\n**Evidence**: The directory structure (`src/model/`, `src/view/`, `src/controller/`) creates clear boundaries between:\n- ML algorithm logic (Model)\n- Dashboard presentation (View)\n- Pipeline orchestration (Controller)\n\n**Impact**: A developer can modify the transformer model implementation (`transformer_summarizer.c`) without touching any Controller or View code. Similarly, adding a new dashboard endpoint requires no Model layer changes.\n\n#### 4.1.2 Modularity and Extensibility via Strategy Pattern\n\n**Evidence** (from `model_strategy.h`, lines 99-104):\n```c\ntypedef struct model_strategy {\n    const char *name;\n    const struct model_strategy_vtable *vptr;  // Virtual table\n    void *impl;\n} model_strategy_t;\n```\n\n**Impact**: New ML strategies can be added by:\n1. Implementing a new strategy file (e.g., `bert_classifier.c`)\n2. Registering it via `ll_strategy_register(\"bert_classifier\", bert_ctor);`\n3. Updating `orchestrator.toml` to specify `active = \"bert_classifier\"`\n\nNo Controller recompilation required - this is a significant MLOps benefit.\n\n#### 4.1.3 Clear High-Level Structure for Complex Systems\n\n**Evidence**: The architecture diagram in `docs/architecture.md` (lines 25-43) provides immediate visual understanding of system organization.\n\n**Impact**: Onboarding new developers is simplified because the MVC pattern is widely understood. The mental model transfers well even though this is a backend system rather than a traditional web application.\n\n#### 4.1.4 Observer Pattern Decouples Components\n\n**Evidence** (from `observer.h`, lines 206-216):\n```c\nstatic inline void observable_notify(const observable_t *observable,\n                                     const observer_event_t *event) {\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < observable->count; ++i) {\n        observer_t *sub = observable->subscribers[i];\n        if (sub && sub->on_event)\n            sub->on_event(event, sub->user_data);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Impact**: Drift detection, logging, dashboard updates, and retraining triggers can all respond to the same event without explicit coupling. Adding a new consumer (e.g., Slack alerts) requires only registering a new observer.\n\n#### 4.1.5 Factory Pattern Enables MLOps Compliance\n\n**Evidence**: The `job_factory.c/h` creates jobs with full metadata for reproducibility:\n- `job_id`, `submitted_by`, `created_at`, `tags[]`\n- JSON serialization for audit trails (`job_factory_to_json()`)\n\n**Impact**: Every training run is traceable, which is essential for ML governance and debugging production issues.\n\n### 4.2 Drawbacks and Architectural Concerns\n\n#### 4.2.1 MVC Mismatch: User Interaction vs. Event-Driven Backend\n\n**Issue**: MVC was designed for interactive user applications with request-response cycles. This ML orchestrator is a long-running, event-driven backend process.\n\n**Evidence of Strain**: The \"View\" (`dashboard_server.c`) is essentially a metrics push server, not a traditional UI. The comment in `dashboard_server.c` (lines 11-18) acknowledges this:\n```c\n/*\n * This module belongs to the View layer and exposes a lightweight HTTP\n * endpoint that streams real-time model-monitoring information to\n * JavaScript dashboards.  The server is intentionally kept simple...\n */\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The View's role is minimal and stretched conceptually\n- No actual \"user input\" handling in the traditional MVC sense\n- The pattern metaphor breaks down when explaining the system to newcomers unfamiliar with this non-standard usage\n\n#### 4.2.2 Controller Bloat (\"Fat Controller\" Anti-Pattern)\n\n**Issue**: The Controller layer contains excessive logic because it must manage:\n- Pipeline orchestration (`pipeline_manager.c`: 359 lines)\n- Drift detection (`drift_detector.c`: 320 lines)\n- Model monitoring (`model_monitor.c`: 365 lines)\n- Task scheduling (`task_scheduler.c`: 400+ lines)\n- Job factory (`job_factory.c`: 300+ lines)\n- Retraining triggers (`retraining_trigger.c`: 415 lines)\n\n**Evidence**: The Controller directory has **6 subdirectories** and **16 files** compared to the Model's **4 subdirectories** and **12 files**.\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The Controller becomes a \"god object\" that knows too much\n- Testing the Controller requires mocking numerous dependencies\n- Changes to orchestration logic risk cascading effects\n\n#### 4.2.3 C Language Limitations for MVC Implementation\n\n**Issue**: MVC frameworks in higher-level languages (Rails, Django, Spring) provide:\n- Automatic dependency injection\n- Data binding between Model and View\n- Declarative routing\n- AOP for cross-cutting concerns\n\nIn C, all of this must be implemented manually.\n\n**Evidence of Manual Wiring** (from `main.c`, lines 563-574):\n```c\nPipelineCtx pipeline_ctx = { .cfg = &cfg,\n                             .registry = &registry,\n                             .strategy = strategy };\n\nScheduler scheduler = { .cfg = &cfg, .pipeline = &pipeline_ctx };\nif (!scheduler_start(&scheduler)) {\n    LOG_ERROR(\"Failed to start scheduler.\");\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- Boilerplate code for wiring components\n- No runtime reflection for flexible component discovery\n- Callback-based Observer pattern is verbose and error-prone (risk of callback hell)\n\n#### 4.2.4 Communication Overhead in C\n\n**Issue**: Model-to-Controller communication via callbacks can be awkward:\n\n**Evidence** (from `drift_detector.c`, lines 213-222):\n```c\n// Provide callback outside of locked section to avoid deadlocks.\ncallback_node_t *tmp_callbacks = g_callbacks;\npthread_mutex_unlock(&g_lock);\n\n// Notify observers\nwhile (tmp_callbacks) {\n    tmp_callbacks->fn(model_id, reason, tmp_callbacks->user_data);\n    tmp_callbacks = tmp_callbacks->next;\n}\n\n// Reacquire lock to reset state.\npthread_mutex_lock(&g_lock);\n```\n\n**Consequences**:\n- Manual lock management to avoid deadlocks\n- No built-in async/await or message queues\n- Potential for subtle concurrency bugs\n\n#### 4.2.5 View Layer Underutilization\n\n**Issue**: The View layer contains only **2 files** (`dashboard_server.c/h`), suggesting it's architecturally under-weighted.\n\n**Evidence**: The View's primary function is to expose `/api/metrics` - a simple JSON endpoint. This could reasonably be a Controller-adjacent utility rather than a separate architectural layer.\n\n**Consequences**:\n- The \"V\" in MVC feels forced in this context\n- Creates artificial separation for minimal benefit\n- May confuse developers expecting a richer View layer\n\n### 4.3 Alternative Patterns to Consider\n\n| Pattern | Suitability | Rationale |\n|---------|------------|-----------|\n| **Hexagonal Architecture (Ports & Adapters)** | High | Better fit for external service integration (LMS API, Feature Store, Model Registry) |\n| **Event-Driven Architecture** | High | Natural fit for drift detection \u2192 retraining workflows |\n| **Pipeline Pattern (alone)** | Medium | Already used internally; could be the primary organizational principle |\n| **Actor Model** | Medium | Mentioned in `docs/architecture.md` (line 116); better for concurrent, message-passing systems |\n\n### 4.4 Summary Assessment\n\n| Aspect | Rating | Justification |\n|--------|--------|--------------|\n| Separation of Concerns | **Good** | Clear boundaries between ML logic, orchestration, and presentation |\n| Extensibility | **Good** | Strategy Pattern allows runtime algorithm swapping |\n| Pattern Fit | **Fair** | MVC's interactive metaphor is stretched for event-driven backends |\n| Controller Complexity | **Concerning** | Risk of \"fat controller\" anti-pattern |\n| Implementation Overhead | **Concerning** | C requires manual wiring that MVC frameworks automate |\n| View Utilization | **Poor** | Minimal View layer suggests pattern mismatch |\n\n**Overall Verdict**: The MVC pattern provides useful organizational structure for this complex system, particularly through its clear directory hierarchy and Strategy Pattern integration. However, the pattern is being used outside its traditional domain (interactive UIs), leading to a stretched View metaphor and bloated Controller. For future evolution, consider migrating toward a Hexagonal or Event-Driven architecture while preserving the existing Strategy and Observer patterns.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conclusion\n\nThe LexiLearn Orchestrator demonstrates a pragmatic adaptation of MVC to the ML orchestration domain. The architecture succeeds in:\n\n1. **Separating ML algorithms** (Model) from **orchestration logic** (Controller) from **external communication** (View)\n2. **Enabling runtime extensibility** through Strategy and Factory patterns\n3. **Decoupling event producers and consumers** via the Observer pattern\n\nHowever, the architecture shows strain in:\n\n1. **The View layer's minimal role**, suggesting MVC's interactive model doesn't fully translate\n2. **Controller complexity**, which risks becoming unmanageable as the system grows\n3. **Manual C-language wiring**, which increases boilerplate compared to framework-supported MVC\n\nFor teams maintaining this system, the recommendations are:\n\n- **Short-term**: Continue using the existing structure but guard against Controller bloat by extracting services\n- **Medium-term**: Introduce message queues (e.g., ZeroMQ) for Model-Controller communication to formalize the event-driven nature\n- **Long-term**: Consider evolving toward Hexagonal Architecture or a pure Event-Sourced design that better matches the system's actual communication patterns\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Key File Reference\n\n| Layer | Key Files | Purpose |\n|-------|-----------|---------|\n| **Model** | `model_strategy.h` | Strategy interface definition |\n| | `model_trainer.h/.c` | Training coordination |\n| | `model_registry.h/.c` | Artifact versioning |\n| | `feature_store_manager.h/.c` | Feature persistence |\n| **View** | `dashboard_server.h/.c` | HTTP metrics endpoint |\n| **Controller** | `orchestrator.h/.c` | Central coordinator |\n| | `pipeline_manager.h/.c` | Pipeline orchestration |\n| | `drift_detector.h/.c` | Drift detection logic |\n| | `model_monitor.h/.c` | Performance surveillance |\n| | `retraining_trigger.h/.c` | Retraining policy |\n| | `observer.h` | Observer Pattern infrastructure |\n| | `job_factory.h/.c` | Factory Pattern for jobs |\n| | `task_scheduler.h/.c` | Task execution engine |\n",

# LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator - Architectural Analysis

## Executive Summary

The LexiLearn Orchestrator is a C-based ML pipeline management system that adopts the Model-View-Controller (MVC) architectural pattern. This document provides a comprehensive analysis of the architecture, mapping components to MVC roles, describing communication pathways, tracing the critical drift-to-retraining workflow, and offering a critical assessment of this architectural choice.

---

## 1. Component Mapping to MVC Roles

### 1.1 Model Layer (`src/model/`)

The Model layer encapsulates all machine learning domain logic, data processing, and state management. It is responsible for the "business logic" of the ML system - the actual algorithms, data transformations, and persistent storage of ML artifacts.

| Directory/File | Purpose | MVC Role Justification |
|---------------|---------|----------------------|
| `src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h` | Strategy Pattern interface for ML algorithms | Defines interchangeable ML algorithm contracts |
| `src/model/ml_models/transformer_summarizer.c/h` | Transformer-based summarization | Concrete ML strategy implementation |
| `src/model/ml_models/ngram_analyzer.c/h` | N-gram-based text analysis | Concrete ML strategy implementation |
| `src/model/ml_models/hybrid_model.c/h` | Ensemble/hybrid modeling | Concrete ML strategy implementation |
| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_trainer.c/h` | Coordinates training workflows | Training execution engine |
| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_registry.c/h` | Model versioning and artifact storage | Persistent state management |
| `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_evaluator.c/h` | Model quality assessment | Evaluation logic |
| `src/model/ml_pipeline/experiment_tracker.c/h` | Experiment lineage tracking | Audit trail ma
... (truncated)
